However, if tracing info is bypassed (e.g. from a 3rd-party system without OTel integration) using `trc.ContextWithSpanContext` with explicit `TraceID` and `SpanID`, a newly created span would be a `nonRecordingSpan`.\n\nThis can be overcome by using `trace.WithSampler(trace.AlwaysSample())` in the tracer provider.\n\n---\n\n#### 5. 🔗 [wavefrontHQ/opentelemetry-examples — Manual Instrumentation in Go](https://github.com/wavefrontHQ/opentelemetry-examples/blob/master/go-example/manual-instrumentation/main.go)\nThe `initTracer()` function sets up a trace exporter via gRPC connection to an OTLP collector, then registers it with a `TracerProvider` using a `BatchSpanProcessor` to aggregate spans before export, and finally sets the global tracer provider via `otel.SetTracerProvider(tracerProvider)`.\n\n---\n\n> **Note:** The `site:github.com/grafana/grafana` filter narrowed the primary result to the `tracing.go` file in the Grafana core repository. Its `Start` method starts a Span and returns it along with a context containing it. The Span is created with the provided name and as a child of any existing span context found in the passed context, configured appropriately by any `SpanOption` passed:\n```go\nfunc (tr *tracer) Start(\n    ctx context.Context,\n    name string,\n    options ...trace.SpanStartOption,\n) (context.Context, trace.Span)\n```\n\n\n---\n\n#### 2. 📄 [`opentelemetry-go/sdk/trace/span.go`](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/main/sdk/trace/span.go)\n`nonRecordingSpan` is a minimal implementation of the OpenTelemetry Span API that wraps a `SpanContext`. It performs no operations other than to return the wrapped `SpanContext` or `TracerProvider` that created it.\n\n---\n\n#### 3. 🐛 [Issue #4621 – `nonRecordingSpan` when using `WithTraceID` + `WithSpanID`](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/issues/4621)\nWhen a fresh span is created from the `Start` method, it produces a normal `recordingSpan`. However, if tracing info is bypassed (e.g., from a third-party system without OTel integration) using `tracer.Start` with `ContextWithSpanContext` and custom `TraceID`/`SpanID`, a newly created span would be a `nonRecordingSpan`.\n\nThis issue can be overcome with `trace.WithSampler(trace.AlwaysSample())` in the tracer provider.\n\n---\n\n#### 4. 💬 [Discussion #2651 – Force sampling when creating a span](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/discussions/2651)\nThe problem arises because the `nonRecordingSpan` created when calling `ContextWithSpanContext` has no `TraceID` nor `SpanID` set, as none were passed to `SpanContextConfig`.\n\nTo always sample the child span, ensure the parent span context contains valid trace and span identifiers and that the `WithLocalParentSampled` option is set to `AlwaysSample` (the default).\n\n---\n\n#### 5. 💬 [Issue #1090 – Helper `trace.Start()` function suggestion](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/issues/1090)\nA suggestion was made to add a helper function `trace.Start` to `api/trace` to aid the happy path of creating a child span within a function.\n\nIf the importing or calling code doesn't use OpenTelemetry and the context contains no span, the span extraction falls back to `NoopSpan` and causes no runtime issues, so functions can be coded to be \"opentelemetry-ready\" even if the caller hasn't hooked in an exporter yet.\n\n---\n\n#### 6. 🐛 [Issue #4727 – Randomly losing spans in production](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/issues/4727)\nIn production, OpenTelemetry was observed losing many traces and spans. Out of 2,588,620 data items processed, only 775,448 traces were found in OpenTelemetry, compared to 2,336,808 in Jaeger.\n\n---\n\n#### 7. 📄 [`opentelemetry-go/sdk/trace/span_processor.go`](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/main/sdk/trace/span_processor.go)\n`SpanProcessor` is a processing pipeline for spans in the trace signal. `SpanProcessors` registered with a `TracerProvider` are called at the start and end of a Span's lifecycle, in the order they are registered.\n\n---\n\n> ⚠️ **Note:** The search did not return results directly from the `prometheus/prometheus` repository. To participate in distributed traces, a `Span` needs to be created for the operation being performed as part of a traced workflow. In its simplest form:\n```go\nvar tracer trace.Tracer\nfunc init() { tracer = otel.Tracer(\"instrumentation/package/name\") }\nfunc operation(ctx context.Context) {\n    var span trace.Span\n    ctx, span = tracer.Start(ctx, \"operation\")\n    defer span.End()\n}\n```\n\n\nThe core span implementation lives in `opentelemetry-go/sdk/trace/span.go`, which is part of the OpenTelemetry Go API and SDK hosted on GitHub.\n\n---\n\n### 🧪 New Span Features (2024–2025)\n\nExperimental **self-observability span** and **batch span processor metrics** have been added in `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/sdk/trace`. The `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/sdk/trace/internal/x` package documentation provides more details.\n\nSemantic conventions have been upgraded from v1.26.0 to v1.34.0 in both `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/sdk/trace` and `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/trace`.\n\n---\n\n### 📦 Prometheus + OpenTelemetry Integration\n\n**Native histogram exemplar support** has been added in `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/exporters/prometheus`.\n\nError handling for dropped data during translation has been improved by using `prometheus.NewInvalidMetric` in `go.opentelemetry.io/otel/exporters/prometheus`. Previously, these cases were only logged and scrapes succeeded. Now, when translation would drop data (e.g., invalid label/value), the exporter emits a `NewInvalidMetric` and Prometheus scrapes fail with HTTP 500 by default. To preserve the prior behavior, configure the handler with `promhttp.HandlerOpts{ ErrorHandling: promhttp.ContinueOnError }`.\n\nA major enhancement is the experimental support for the **OTLP Metrics protocol**, which allows Prometheus to receive metrics from OpenTelemetry exporters via the `/api/v1/otlp/v1/metrics` endpoint — improving interoperability and aligning Prometheus with OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n\n---\n\n### 🌐 SpanProcessor Reporting Prometheus Metrics\n\nThere is an active Go project described as **\"An OpenTelemetry SpanProcessor reporting tracing flow metrics\"**, tagged with `metrics`, `prometheus`, `tracing`, `otel`, `opentelemetry`, and `opentelemetry-go`, last updated in **June 2025**.\n\n---\n\n### 🔗 Key Links\n\n| Resource | URL |\n|---|---|\n| OpenTelemetry Go SDK | [github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go) |\n| `sdk/trace/span.go` | [opentelemetry-go/sdk/trace/span.go](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/blob/main/sdk/trace/span.go) |\n| OTel Trace Go pkg | [pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/trace](https://pkg.go.dev/go.opentelemetry.io/otel/trace) |\n| OTel Go Releases | [github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/releases](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-go/releases) |\n\n---\n\n> 💡 **Note:** If you are specifically looking for tracing/span-related `.go` files **within** the `prometheus/prometheus` repository itself (e.g., `util/telemetry/` or similar), I can do a more targeted search. It embeds `services.NamedService` and implements the `Tracer` interface with methods for span injection into HTTP headers.\n\nThe **tracerProvider** interface wraps `trace.TracerProvider` and requires a `Shutdown` method for cleanup.\n\n## Tracer Initialization Patterns\n\nThree exporter implementations are supported:\n\n1. **Jaeger**: Configured via `initJaegerTracerProvider()` with support for both agent (host:port) and collector (HTTP URL) endpoints\n2. **OTLP**: Initialized through `initOTLPTracerProvider()` with gRPC transport and optional TLS\n3. **Noop**: A no-operation provider for disabled tracing\n\nThe initialization flow:\n- `ProvideService()` creates a TracingService instance\n- `initOpentelemetryTracer()` routes to the appropriate provider based on configuration\n- Each provider applies a sampler (const, probabilistic, rateLimiting, or remote)\n\n## Sampling Implementation\n\nThe custom **rateLimiter** sampler implements token-bucket rate limiting with thread-safe balance tracking. It recalculates balance based on elapsed time and RPS configuration, deciding whether to sample individual spans.\n\n## Span Management\n\n**Error Recording**: The `Error()` function sets span status to error, records exceptions, and extracts Grafana-specific error IDs as attributes.\n\n**Span Creation**: The `Start()` function creates spans only when a span already exists in the context, delegating to its tracer provider.\n\n**Propagation**: The `Inject()` method adds trace context to HTTP headers using configured propagators (W3C TraceContext/Baggage or Jaeger format).\n\n## Utility Functions\n\n- `TraceIDFromContext()` extracts trace IDs with optional sampling validation\n- `ServerTimingForSpan()` formats W3C Server-Timing header values\n- `Errorf()` wraps error creation and span recording"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"725a373d-20eb-485c-a5e7-c10ba110c3b5","uuid":"2d545dc2-dba9-4833-9f4d-e314c4d04413","tool_use_result":{"bytes":12591,"code":200,"codeText":"OK","result":"# Tracing Package Overview\n\nThis Go package implements OpenTelemetry-based distributed tracing for Grafana with support for multiple exporters and propagators.\n\n## Core Structures\n\n**TracingService** is the main service that manages tracer initialization and lifecycle. Better Together | OpenTelemetry\",\"url\":\"https://opentelemetry.io/blog/2024/prom-and-otel/\"},{\"title\":\"Prometheus and OpenMetrics Compatibility | OpenTelemetry\",\"url\":\"https://opentelemetry.io/docs/specs/otel/compatibility/prometheus_and_openmetrics/\"},{\"title\":\"Telemetry with OpenTelemetry, Prometheus and Jaeger | by Guilherme Pereira | Medium\",\"url\":\"https://medium.com/@guilospanck/telemetry-with-opentelemetry-prometheus-and-jaeger-46a2d9dec86b\"}]\n\nHere is a comprehensive summary of the search results on **Prometheus, OpenTelemetry, tracing spans, scraping, retrieval, and storage**:\n\n---\n\n## 🔭 Prometheus & OpenTelemetry: Tracing, Spans, Scraping, and Storage\n\n### 1. 🔗 How Prometheus and OpenTelemetry Work Together\n\nObservability in modern systems often starts with Prometheus — the tool most developers and operators rely on to scrape and expose metrics from their applications and infrastructure. As teams adopt OpenTelemetry for unified telemetry collection, the question becomes: how do you bring all that Prometheus data into the OpenTelemetry world?\n\nThat's where the **Prometheus receiver** comes in. It lets the OpenTelemetry Collector act like a Prometheus server by scraping any Prometheus-compatible endpoint, then converting the metrics into the OpenTelemetry Protocol (OTLP).\n\n---\n\n### 2. 🕸️ Tracing Spans & Exemplars in Prometheus/OTel\n\nThe Prometheus receiver accepts **exemplars** coming in Prometheus format and converts them to OTLP format. Labels with key `span_id` in Prometheus exemplars are set as OTLP span IDs, and labels with key `trace_id` are set as trace IDs.\n\nAccording to the OpenTelemetry compatibility spec, Prometheus Exemplars **must** use the `trace_id` and `span_id` keys for the trace and span IDs, respectively. Timestamps must be added as timestamps on the Prometheus exemplar, and filtered attributes must be added as labels.\n\nThe Trace ID and Span ID should be retrieved from the `trace_id` and `span_id` label keys, respectively. All labels not used for trace and span IDs must be added to the OpenTelemetry exemplar as attributes.\n\n---\n\n### 3. 🔄 Scrape & Retrieval Pipeline\n\nA **Scrape** is the action of collecting Metrics through an HTTP request from a targeted instance, parsing the response, and ingesting the collected samples to storage.\n\n**ScrapeLoop** is the actual scrape pipeline, performing the main scraping and ingestion logic. Each scraping cycle is triggered by a configured interval.\n\n`StorageAppender` is an abstraction of the metric storage, which can be a filesystem, a database, or a remote endpoint. For the OpenTelemetry Prometheus receiver, this is the interface implemented to provide a customized storage appender backed by a metrics sink.\n\n---\n\n### 4. 📦 Storage & Architecture (GitHub: opentelemetry-collector-contrib)\n\nThe original Prometheus receiver of OpenTelemetry took the approach of using Prometheus' own scraper's source code as a library. The original implementation had many glitches that couldn't be fixed by small patches. The new Prometheus receiver follows the same idea of leveraging Prometheus source code, but with a proper implementation.\n\nThe Prometheus receiver maps Prometheus metrics to OpenTelemetry proto-based metrics, respecting the original metric name, value, timestamp, and tags. It doesn't need to provide a one-to-one mapping, since supported metric types differ between the two systems.\n\nThe receiver uses exporter-level batching via `sending_queue.batch` to improve efficiency when multiple scrapes occur, and exports metrics to both an OTLP endpoint and Prometheus remote write endpoint. The Prometheus receiver also **automatically converts native histograms to OpenTelemetry exponential histograms**.\n\n---\n\n### 5. 🧩 Span Metrics: Bridging Traces and Prometheus\n\nBoth metrics and tracings can derive from the same **spans** that you instrument, and there are many ways to instrument an application.\n\nThe OpenTelemetry Collector supports a **spanmetrics connector**, which converts trace spans into Prometheus-compatible metrics (e.g., request rates, error rates, duration histograms), which Prometheus can then scrape. The OpenTelemetry Collector is added as a target within Prometheus, using the standard port for Prometheus metrics (9464).\n\n---\n\n### 6. ⚠️ Limitations of the Prometheus Receiver\n\nWhile the Prometheus receiver is designed to act as a near drop-in replacement for a Prometheus server, it doesn't implement every feature. Its goal is focused: to scrape metrics and feed them into the OpenTelemetry pipeline. Features related to alerting, long-term storage, or query evaluation remain outside its scope.\n\nTo set up the OpenTelemetry Collector for native Prometheus target discovery, you should exclude sections like Alerting, Storage, Recording Rules, Tracing, and Remote Read/Write from the Prometheus configuration.\n\n---\n\n### 📚 Key References\n- **GitHub (OTel Collector Contrib - Design):** [prometheusreceiver/DESIGN.md](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-collector-contrib/blob/main/receiver/prometheusreceiver/DESIGN.md)\n- **GitHub (OTel Collector Contrib - README):** [prometheusreceiver/README.md](https://github.com/open-telemetry/opentelemetry-collector-contrib/blob/main/receiver/prometheusreceiver/README.md)\n- **OpenTelemetry Docs:** [Prometheus & OpenMetrics Compatibility](https://opentelemetry.io/docs/specs/otel/compatibility/prometheus_and_openmetrics/)\n- **OpenTelemetry Blog:** [Prometheus and OpenTelemetry – Better Together](https://opentelemetry.io/blog/2024/prom-and-otel/)\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"725a373d-20eb-485c-a5e7-c10ba110c3b5","uuid":"d555c57c-8206-4f0a-88b5-9e1b290edd8d","tool_use_result":{"query":"prometheus prometheus github tracing span opentelemetry scrape retrieval storage","results":[{"tool_use_id":"srvtoolu_012zinpEbai84x2BezcRFZmN","content":[{"title":"Collecting Prometheus Metrics with the OpenTelemetry Collector · Dash0","url":"https://www.dash0.com/guides/opentelemetry-prometheus-receiver"},{"title":"Prometheus Receiver -
